The [3mCollected Works of [0mKarl Marx and Frederick Engels present Engelsโs works and letters in English translation (or in the 
original English) in approximately 50 volumes. The first volume appeared in 1975, and the publishers are Progress of Moscow, 
Lawrence & Wishart of London, and International of New York, referred to below as the Progress consortium. All the major works of 
Engels (and the joint works with Marx) mentioned in the text are available in Progress editions, and [3mThe Condition of the Working 
Class in England [0mis also translated and edited by W. O. Henderson and W. H. Chaloner (2nd edn., Blackwell, Oxford, 1971; Stanford 
University Press, 1968). 

The [3mSelected Works [0mof Karl Marx and Frederick Engels in one volume was first published in 1968 and has been reprinted by the 
Progress consortium; of Engelsโs major works it includes [3mSocialism: Utopian and Scientific and The Origin of the Family, Private 
Property and the State, with Ludwig Feuerbach and the End of Classical German Philosophy [0m. The [3mSelected Works [0min two volumes from 
the same publishers includes more of Engelsโs shorter writings, such as the 1859 review โKarl Marx: A Contribution to the Critique 
of Political Economyโ and โOn Authorityโ. [3mEngels: Selected Writings [0m, edited by W. O. Henderson (Penguin, Harmondsworth, and 
Baltimore, Md, 1967) contains selections from [3mThe Condition of the Working Class in England [0mand the full text of the โOutlines of 
a Critique of Political Economyโ, as well as other economic, historical, philosophical and military writings. [3mEngels as Military 
Critic [0m, edited by W. O. Henderson and W. H. Chaloner (Manchester University Press, 1959; Greenwood Press, Westport, Conn., 1976), 
presents a selection of lesser-known articles of the 1860s. [3mGerman Revolutions [0m, edited by Leonard Krieger (University of Chicago 
Press, 1968), includes [3mThe Peasant War in Germany and Germany: Revolution and Counter-Revolution [0m. 

[1mุฃุนูุงู ุนูู [0m

I am indebted to the factual material collected and very well documented in W. O. Hendersonโs [3mThe Life of Friedrich Engels [0min two 
volumes (Frank Cass, London, and Portland, Or., 1976). Gustav Mayerโs two-volume biography in German is published as [3mFriedrich 
Engels [0min an abridged English translation by Gilbert and Helen Highet, edited by R. H. S. Crossman (Chapman & Hall, London, 1936; 
H. Fertig, New York, 1969). David McLellanโs Modern Masters [3mEngels [0m(Fontana/Collins, Glasgow, 1977; Penguin, Baltimore, Md., 1978) 
presents a brief account of Engelsโs life and works. 

Engelsโs major works are discussed in Fritz Novaโs [3mFriedrich Engels: His Contributions to Political Theory [0m(Vision Press, London, 
1968; Philosophical Library, New York, 1967). [3mEngels, Manchester and the Working Class [0mby Steven Marcus (Random House, New York, 
1974) presents an analysis of the work from a literary point of view. Engelsโs early works on British politics feature in Michael 
Levin, [3mThe Condition of England Question: Carlyle, Mill, Engels [0m(Macmillan, London, and St Martinโs, New York, 1998). His late 
work [3mThe Origin of the Family, Private Property and the State [0mhas become a classic of Marxistfeminism and gender studies; see 
Janet Sayers, Mary Ann Evans, Naneke Redclift (eds.), [3mEngels Revisited: New Feminist Essays [0m(Tavistock, London, 1987), and two 
articles by Terrell Carver, โEngelsโs Feminismโ, [3mHistory of Political Thought [0m, 6/3 (1985), 479โ89, and โTheorizing Men in 
Engelsโs [3mOrigin of the Family [0mโ, [3mMasculinities [0m, 2/1 (1994), 67โ77. There are two recent edited volumes offering critical 
discussions of a wide range of topics that Engels was concerned with: Christopher J. Arthur (ed.), [3mEngels Today: A Centenary 
Appreciation [0m(Macmillan, Basingstoke, and St Martinโs, New York, 1996), and Manfred B. Steger and Terrell Carver (eds), [3mEngels 
after Marx [0m(Pennsylvania State University Press, University Park, Pa., 1999). The Marx-Engels relationship is considered in Norman 
Levine, [3mThe Tragic Deception: Marx contra Engels [0m(Clio Books, Oxford, and Santa Barbara, Calif., 1975). I have also published [3mMarx 
and Engels: The Intellectual Relationship [0m(Wheatsheaf Books, Brighton, and Bloomington, Ind., Indiana University Press, 1983), and 
a biographical study [3mFriedrich Engels: His Life and Thought [0m(Macmillan, Basingstoke, 1989, and St Martinโs, New York, 1990). 

The relationship of Engels to Marxism is discussed in George Lichtheimโs [3mMarxism: An Historical and Critical Study [0m(2nd edn., 
Routledge & Kegan Paul, 1968; Praeger, 1965), and in Richard N. Hunt, [3mThe Political Ideas of Marx and Engels [0m, vol. 1, [3mMarxism and 
Totalitarian Democracy [0m(Macmillan, London, 1975; University of Pittsburgh Press, 1974). This topic is covered in three classic 
studies: Leszek Kolakowski, [3mMain Currents of Marxism [0m, translated by P. S. Falla, vol. 1 (Oxford University Press, Oxford and New 
York, 1978); David McLellan, [3mMarxism after Marx [0m(Macmillan, London, 1979; Harper & Row, New York, 1980); and Alvin W. Gouldner, [3m
The Two Marxisms [0m(Macmillan, London; Seabury Press, New York, 1980). Two recent studies on this theme are S. H. Rigby, [3mEngels and 
the Formation of Marxism: History, Dialectics and Revolution [0m(Manchester University Press, Manchester and New York, 1992), and J. 
D. Hunley, [3mThe Life and Thought of Friedrich Engels: A Reinterpretation [0m(Yale University Press,New Haven, and London, 1991). 

Four articles of interest in which Engelsโs work is discussed are: Terrell Carver, โMarx, Engels, and Dialecticsโ, [3mPolitical 
Studies [0m, 28/3 (September 1980), 353โ63; Gareth Stedman Jones, โEngels and the End of Classical German Philosophyโ, [3mNew Left 
Review [0m, 79 (May-June 1973), 17โ36; the same authorโs โEngels and the Genesis of Marxismโ, [3mNew Left Review [0m, 106 
(November-December 1977), 79โ104; and Paul Thomas, โMarx and Scienceโ, [3mPolitical Studies [0m, 24/1 (March 1976), 1โ23. The last-named 
article has been particularly helpful to me in working out my views on Engels. 

There is now an excellent Marx-Engels bibliography in English: Cecil L. Eubanks, [3mKarl Marx and Friedrich Engels: An Analytical 
Bibliography [0m(Garland Press, London and New York, 1977).
